          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }

          width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





The `--disable-print-preview` flag was in general not required to reproduce the issue. I have seen the crash happening without that flag. However, I kept it during testcase minimization and I might have lost reproducibility without the flag because it triggered the crash faster during that process.



<span class="line"><!---->The `--disable-print-preview` flag was in general not required to reproduce the issue. I have seen the crash happening without that flag. However, I kept it during testcase minimization and I might have lost reproducibility without the flag because it triggered the crash faster during that process.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





The `--disable-print-preview` flag was in general not required to reproduce the issue. I have seen the crash happening without that flag. However, I kept it during testcase minimization and I might have lost reproducibility without the flag because it triggered the crash faster during that process.



<span class="line"><!---->The `--disable-print-preview` flag was in general not required to reproduce the issue. I have seen the crash happening without that flag. However, I kept it during testcase minimization and I might have lost reproducibility without the flag because it triggered the crash faster during that process.<!----></span>

Please be sure to put ASAN_OPTIONS env variable, or it won't repro.



<span class="line"><!---->Please be sure to put ASAN_OPTIONS env variable, or it won't repro.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Here's what I did



<span class="line"><!---->Here's what I did<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





ASAN_OPTIONS=log_path=/tmp/asan.log:symbolize=1:abort_on_error=1:allocator_may_return_null=1:alloc_dealloc_mismatch=0:allow_user_poisoning=1:allow_user_segv_handler=1:check_initialization_order=1:check_malloc_usable_size=0:detect_invalid_pointer_pairs=2:detect_leaks=0:detect_odr_violation=1:detect_stack_use_after_return=1:detect_stack_use_after_scope=1:fast_unwind_on_fatal=1:handle_abort=1:handle_segv=1:handle_sigbus=1:handle_sigfpe=1:handle_sigill=1:max_uar_stack_size_log=16:print_cmdline=1:print_scariness=1:print_summary=1:print_suppressions=0:redzone=16:strict_init_order=1:strict_memcmp=1:strict_string_checks=1:use_sigaltstack=1 ./out/Asan/Chromium.app/Contents/MacOS/Chromium --disable-print-preview ~/Desktop/print.html

I can reproduce on my iMac Pro with macOS 11.6.4 (20G417).



<span class="line"><!---->I can reproduce on my iMac Pro with macOS 11.6.4 (20G417).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Given this seems like an issue with Apple’s print dialog, it seems to me to have the next step be a reproduction with a sample app that does printing. A bug report to Apple saying “this simple two-line app built with asan shows a heap buffer overflow” is better than one that starts by saying to build Chromium with asan.



<span class="line"><!---->Given this seems like an issue with Apple’s print dialog, it seems to me to have the next step be a reproduction with a sample app that does printing. A bug report to Apple saying “this simple two-line app built with asan shows a heap buffer overflow” is better than one that starts by saying to build Chromium with asan.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I will work on that. Meanwhile, the stack shows that the PDF being mis-parsed is being used to draw a button, which implies it’s not under attacker control. Determining what PDF is being drawn might be another avenue of investigation.



<span class="line"><!---->I will work on that. Meanwhile, the stack shows that the PDF being mis-parsed is being used to draw a button, which implies it’s not under attacker control. Determining what PDF is being drawn might be another avenue of investigation.<!----></span>

I briefly went down the second rabbit hole and executed this under lldb. Attaching the log.



<span class="line"><!---->I briefly went down the second rabbit hole and executed this under lldb. Attaching the log.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When it hit the SIGABRT I backed up the stack to `CGPDFDocumentCreateWithProvider` which starts like:



<span class="line"><!---->When it hit the SIGABRT I backed up the stack to `CGPDFDocumentCreateWithProvider` which starts like:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





   _CGPDFDocumentCreateWithProvider:



<span class="line"><!---->   _CGPDFDocumentCreateWithProvider:<!----></span>



<br>





00007fff24e45553         push       rbp



<span class="line"><!---->00007fff24e45553         push       rbp<!----></span>



<br>





00007fff24e45554         mov        rbp, rsp



<span class="line"><!---->00007fff24e45554         mov        rbp, rsp<!----></span>



<br>





00007fff24e45557         push       r15



<span class="line"><!---->00007fff24e45557         push       r15<!----></span>



<br>





00007fff24e45559         push       r14



<span class="line"><!---->00007fff24e45559         push       r14<!----></span>



<br>





00007fff24e4555b         push       rbx



<span class="line"><!---->00007fff24e4555b         push       rbx<!----></span>



<br>





00007fff24e4555c         push       rax



<span class="line"><!---->00007fff24e4555c         push       rax<!----></span>



<br>





00007fff24e4555d         mov        r14, rdi



<span class="line"><!---->00007fff24e4555d         mov        r14, rdi<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I took a stab, and yes, r14 was the CGDataProvider that was passed in. Unfortunately, printing the description wasn’t helpful, so I called CGDataProviderCopyData to see what the failing data looked like, to see if it was our PDF or theirs. That got me the data, so I saved it. I’m attaching it too.



<span class="line"><!---->I took a stab, and yes, r14 was the CGDataProvider that was passed in. Unfortunately, printing the description wasn’t helpful, so I called CGDataProviderCopyData to see what the failing data looked like, to see if it was our PDF or theirs. That got me the data, so I saved it. I’m attaching it too.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This seems to confirm my reading of the stacktrace implying that it was a failure to read the PDF that contained the image of the button used in the print dialog.



<span class="line"><!---->This seems to confirm my reading of the stacktrace implying that it was a failure to read the PDF that contained the image of the button used in the print dialog.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It’s definitely something we want to report to Apple, as there’s clearly a bug in their PDF parser and they shouldn’t be reading past the buffer when they show a print dialog. But I don’t see this as being critical priority.



<span class="line"><!---->It’s definitely something we want to report to Apple, as there’s clearly a bug in their PDF parser and they shouldn’t be reading past the buffer when they show a print dialog. But I don’t see this as being critical priority.<!----></span>

comment 34



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c34"><!---->comment 34<!----></a>





.



<span class="line"><!---->.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This system print dialog is only directly triggerable by JavaScript because of the use of the `--disable-print-preview` commandline flag. That flag causes Chrome to use the system print dialog rather than our own print preview dialog.



<span class="line"><!---->This system print dialog is only directly triggerable by JavaScript because of the use of the `--disable-print-preview` commandline flag. That flag causes Chrome to use the system print dialog rather than our own print preview dialog.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





However, without that commandline flag, what happens is that the JavaScript print command triggers our print preview dialog, not the system one, and Chrome does not do that OOB read. If the user manually clicks the “More settings” toggle in our print preview dialog, and clicks the “Print using system dialog...” button, then the system dialog is opened and the OOB read happens, but I don’t believe that manipulating items in our print preview dialog is within the capability of JavaScript to do.



<span class="line"><!---->However, without that commandline flag, what happens is that the JavaScript print command triggers our print preview dialog, not the system one, and Chrome does not do that OOB read. If the user manually clicks the “More settings” toggle in our print preview dialog, and clicks the “Print using system dialog...” button, then the system dialog is opened and the OOB read happens, but I don’t believe that manipulating items in our print preview dialog is within the capability of JavaScript to do.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Comment 0



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c0"><!---->Comment 0<!----></a>





 states that the `--disable-print-preview` commandline flag isn’t necessary. However, without that flag, UI interaction is needed to trigger the opening of the system print dialog. Have you been able to reproduce this ASAN OOB read with no UI interaction and without that flag?



<span class="line"><!----> states that the `--disable-print-preview` commandline flag isn’t necessary. However, without that flag, UI interaction is needed to trigger the opening of the system print dialog. Have you been able to reproduce this ASAN OOB read with no UI interaction and without that flag?<!----></span>

We typically have bugs like this stay open with ExternalDependency. I don’t know how our security machinery takes that, though.



<span class="line"><!---->We typically have bugs like this stay open with ExternalDependency. I don’t know how our security machinery takes that, though.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Dana, alas no. This is the OS’s PDF parser parsing a PDF that contains system UI graphics, where the call graph is entirely within OS code. In general we can’t patch out OS function implementations (code signing, etc). Methods implemented in Objective-C could be swizzled, though in the two call stacks (attached) they go through different paths, and it’s not clear how many other paths there are.



<span class="line"><!---->Dana, alas no. This is the OS’s PDF parser parsing a PDF that contains system UI graphics, where the call graph is entirely within OS code. In general we can’t patch out OS function implementations (code signing, etc). Methods implemented in Objective-C could be swizzled, though in the two call stacks (attached) they go through different paths, and it’s not clear how many other paths there are.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





But if we went down the swizzle route, we could swizzle say, -[_CUIThemePDFRendition _initWithCSIHeader:] and -[_NSPDFDocument initWithData:] (since we don’t use the system PDF functionality). However, what then? I’m pretty sure that those are called all the time, so if we crash this would likely make Chrome unusable. What’s the implication of returning nil? I’d imagine that at best you then have huge blank areas of the screen, and at worst, crashes. And I don’t see how we could substitute in a compatible working PDF implementation in a way that would work.



<span class="line"><!---->But if we went down the swizzle route, we could swizzle say, -[_CUIThemePDFRendition _initWithCSIHeader:] and -[_NSPDFDocument initWithData:] (since we don’t use the system PDF functionality). However, what then? I’m pretty sure that those are called all the time, so if we crash this would likely make Chrome unusable. What’s the implication of returning nil? I’d imagine that at best you then have huge blank areas of the screen, and at worst, crashes. And I don’t see how we could substitute in a compatible working PDF implementation in a way that would work.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





From what I see, this is basically a OOB read for every bit of the macOS UI for which they use a PDF as the vector icon, which is huge swaths of the UI. I can’t think of anything we could do to mitigate it.



<span class="line"><!---->From what I see, this is basically a OOB read for every bit of the macOS UI for which they use a PDF as the vector icon, which is huge swaths of the UI. I can’t think of anything we could do to mitigate it.<!----></span>

Apple has responded; they believe it is a false positive.



<span class="line"><!---->Apple has responded; they believe it is a false positive.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





-----



<span class="line"><!---->-----<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This reproduces only with strict_string_checks=1. That’s the only ASAN option that needs to be set.



<span class="line"><!---->This reproduces only with strict_string_checks=1. That’s the only ASAN option that needs to be set.<!----></span>



<br>





The line of code flagged by ASAN is (with pdf_object_name expanded):



<span class="line"><!---->The line of code flagged by ASAN is (with pdf_object_name expanded):<!----></span>



<br>





            



<span class="line"><!---->            <!----></span>



<br>





(lexer->object)->u.name = strndup(lexer->buffer, lexer->token_length);



<span class="line"><!---->(lexer-&gt;object)-&gt;u.name = strndup(lexer-&gt;buffer, lexer-&gt;token_length);<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When it reproduces:



<span class="line"><!---->When it reproduces:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





(lldb) p lexer->token_length



<span class="line"><!---->(lldb) p lexer-&gt;token_length<!----></span>



<br>





(size_t) $7 = 4



<span class="line"><!---->(size_t) $7 = 4<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





(lldb) expression (size_t)malloc_size(lexer->buffer)



<span class="line"><!---->(lldb) expression (size_t)malloc_size(lexer-&gt;buffer)<!----></span>



<br>





(size_t) $6 = 128



<span class="line"><!---->(size_t) $6 = 128<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The size of lexer->buffer is guaranteed to be bigger than lexer->token_length.



<span class="line"><!---->The size of lexer-&gt;buffer is guaranteed to be bigger than lexer-&gt;token_length.<!----></span>



<br>





If I NULL-terminate lexer->buffer, the ASAN failure goes away.



<span class="line"><!---->If I NULL-terminate lexer-&gt;buffer, the ASAN failure goes away.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We believe this is an ASAN false positive. It’s as if ASAN considers strndup to work like strdup.



<span class="line"><!---->We believe this is an ASAN false positive. It’s as if ASAN considers strndup to work like strdup.<!----></span>

OK, I believe I found it at 



<span class="line"><!---->OK, I believe I found it at <!----></span>





https://github.com/llvm/llvm-project/blob/main/compiler-rt/lib/sanitizer_common/sanitizer_common_interceptors.inc#L380



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/llvm/llvm-project/blob/main/compiler-rt/lib/sanitizer_common/sanitizer_common_interceptors.inc#L380"><!---->https://github.com/llvm/llvm-project/blob/main/compiler-rt/lib/sanitizer_common/sanitizer_common_interceptors.inc#L380<!----></a>





 :



<span class="line"><!----> :<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





#ifndef COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_STRNDUP_IMPL



<span class="line"><!---->#ifndef COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_STRNDUP_IMPL<!----></span>



<br>





#define COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_STRNDUP_IMPL(ctx, s, size)                         \



<span class="line"><!---->#define COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_STRNDUP_IMPL(ctx, s, size)                         \<!----></span>



<br>





  COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_ENTER(ctx, strndup, s, size);                            \



<span class="line"><!---->  COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_ENTER(ctx, strndup, s, size);                            \<!----></span>



<br>





  uptr copy_length = internal_strnlen(s, size);                               \



<span class="line"><!---->  uptr copy_length = internal_strnlen(s, size);                               \<!----></span>



<br>





  char *new_mem = (char *)WRAP(malloc)(copy_length + 1);                      \



<span class="line"><!---->  char *new_mem = (char *)WRAP(malloc)(copy_length + 1);                      \<!----></span>



<br>





  if (common_flags()->intercept_strndup) {                                    \



<span class="line"><!---->  if (common_flags()-&gt;intercept_strndup) {                                    \<!----></span>



<br>





    COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_READ_STRING(ctx, s, Min(size, copy_length + 1));       \



<span class="line"><!---->    COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_READ_STRING(ctx, s, Min(size, copy_length + 1));       \<!----></span>



<br>





  }                                                                           \



<span class="line"><!---->  }                                                                           \<!----></span>



<br>





  COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_COPY_STRING(ctx, new_mem, s, copy_length);               \



<span class="line"><!---->  COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_COPY_STRING(ctx, new_mem, s, copy_length);               \<!----></span>



<br>





  internal_memcpy(new_mem, s, copy_length);                                   \



<span class="line"><!---->  internal_memcpy(new_mem, s, copy_length);                                   \<!----></span>



<br>





  new_mem[copy_length] = '\0';                                                \



<span class="line"><!---->  new_mem[copy_length] = '\0';                                                \<!----></span>



<br>





  return new_mem;



<span class="line"><!---->  return new_mem;<!----></span>



<br>





#endif



<span class="line"><!---->#endif<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The error from ASan is



<span class="line"><!---->The error from ASan is<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





READ of size 129 at 0x60c000066e40 thread T0



<span class="line"><!---->READ of size 129 at 0x60c000066e40 thread T0<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So I guess that’s the `COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_READ_STRING` line. There are two cases here:



<span class="line"><!---->So I guess that’s the `COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_READ_STRING` line. There are two cases here:<!----></span>



<br>





- `internal_strnlen` is capped by `s`’s length, in which case `copy_length` is `s`’s length, we call `COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_READ_STRING` with `copy_length + 1`, which copies the null byte.



<span class="line"><!---->- `internal_strnlen` is capped by `s`’s length, in which case `copy_length` is `s`’s length, we call `COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_READ_STRING` with `copy_length + 1`, which copies the null byte.<!----></span>



<br>





- `internal_strnlen` is capped by the `size`, in which case `copy_length` is `size`, we call `COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_READ_STRING` with `size`, and then tack a null byte at the end.



<span class="line"><!---->- `internal_strnlen` is capped by the `size`, in which case `copy_length` is `size`, we call `COMMON_INTERCEPTOR_READ_STRING` with `size`, and then tack a null byte at the end.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I don’t see how this is consistent with Apple’s report of the values at the callsite.



<span class="line"><!---->I don’t see how this is consistent with Apple’s report of the values at the callsite.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Do people agree? How can I gently call Apple out to say, “Here’s the source of ASan. We don’t believe your claim that this is a false-positive from ASan. Please dig harder.”



<span class="line"><!---->Do people agree? How can I gently call Apple out to say, “Here’s the source of ASan. We don’t believe your claim that this is a false-positive from ASan. Please dig harder.”<!----></span>

OP:



<span class="line"><!---->OP:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Apple points out that this fails with “strict_string_checks=1” and that’s the key to the mystery here.



<span class="line"><!---->Apple points out that this fails with “strict_string_checks=1” and that’s the key to the mystery here.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





What is “strict_string_checks”? As per the docs¹, “if true, check that string arguments are properly null-terminated”. What you may not have realized is that they mean _all_ string arguments.



<span class="line"><!---->What is “strict_string_checks”? As per the docs¹, “if true, check that string arguments are properly null-terminated”. What you may not have realized is that they mean _all_ string arguments.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Here is some pseudocode for what Apple is doing:



<span class="line"><!---->Here is some pseudocode for what Apple is doing:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





---8<---



<span class="line"><!---->---8&lt;---<!----></span>



<br>





const char* some_chars = /* from a pdf, parse out some non-zero-terminated char data */



<span class="line"><!---->const char* some_chars = /* from a pdf, parse out some non-zero-terminated char data */<!----></span>



<br>





size_t some_size = /* from a pdf, parse out the length of the char data from the previous line */



<span class="line"><!---->size_t some_size = /* from a pdf, parse out the length of the char data from the previous line */<!----></span>



<br>





char* new_string = strndup(some_chars, some_size);



<span class="line"><!---->char* new_string = strndup(some_chars, some_size);<!----></span>



<br>





---8<---



<span class="line"><!---->---8&lt;---<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In this use case, the first parameter to `strndup` is _never_ null-terminated, and Apple is using `strndup` to create a copy of a string that has a null terminator.



<span class="line"><!---->In this use case, the first parameter to `strndup` is _never_ null-terminated, and Apple is using `strndup` to create a copy of a string that has a null terminator.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Is this legal, valid code? It depends on where you look, but probably not.



<span class="line"><!---->Is this legal, valid code? It depends on where you look, but probably not.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In POSIX² the documentation talks about the “string pointed to by s”. I can’t find a definition of “string” in POSIX, but I believe this implicitly requires the first parameter to `strndup` to be null-terminated.



<span class="line"><!---->In POSIX² the documentation talks about the “string pointed to by s”. I can’t find a definition of “string” in POSIX, but I believe this implicitly requires the first parameter to `strndup` to be null-terminated.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In C23³ the documentation is very explicit: “src - pointer to the null-terminated byte string to duplicate”.



<span class="line"><!---->In C23³ the documentation is very explicit: “src - pointer to the null-terminated byte string to duplicate”.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So, yes, this is not valid code. They are (arguably) misusing `strndup` to create a null-terminated string from a non-null-terminated string.



<span class="line"><!---->So, yes, this is not valid code. They are (arguably) misusing `strndup` to create a null-terminated string from a non-null-terminated string.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





However, this code does not ever perform an OOB read on its own.



<span class="line"><!---->However, this code does not ever perform an OOB read on its own.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Apple is wrong in saying that there’s a bug in ASan. It is correctly catching their invalid use of the `strndup` API. However, they are correct in saying that the “strict_string_checks” flag in ASan _causes_ the OOB read. Without that flag, there is no OOB read.



<span class="line"><!---->Apple is wrong in saying that there’s a bug in ASan. It is correctly catching their invalid use of the `strndup` API. However, they are correct in saying that the “strict_string_checks” flag in ASan _causes_ the OOB read. Without that flag, there is no OOB read.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Is “strict_string_checks” buggy? The authors of ASan have made it clear that they do not believe so⁴.



<span class="line"><!---->Is “strict_string_checks” buggy? The authors of ASan have made it clear that they do not believe so⁴.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Is “strict_string_checks” _useful_? I can’t say that it is. It’s unlike all the other sanitizer flags, being opinionated. All the other sanitizer flags are sensing and exposing genuine bad memory use that otherwise would not be noticed. “strict_string_checks”, however, will _cause_ an OOB read  to indicate theoretically invalid use of an API that without ASan does not read out of bounds.



<span class="line"><!---->Is “strict_string_checks” _useful_? I can’t say that it is. It’s unlike all the other sanitizer flags, being opinionated. All the other sanitizer flags are sensing and exposing genuine bad memory use that otherwise would not be noticed. “strict_string_checks”, however, will _cause_ an OOB read  to indicate theoretically invalid use of an API that without ASan does not read out of bounds.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If you are writing code against the POSIX/C string APIs, and you want to ensure you are strictly obeying the documented requirements for parameters, then perhaps “strict_string_checks” can be useful. But in every other case, I would reconsider using it.



<span class="line"><!---->If you are writing code against the POSIX/C string APIs, and you want to ensure you are strictly obeying the documented requirements for parameters, then perhaps “strict_string_checks” can be useful. But in every other case, I would reconsider using it.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->¹ <!----></span>





https://github.com/google/sanitizers/wiki/AddressSanitizerFlags



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/google/sanitizers/wiki/AddressSanitizerFlags"><!---->https://github.com/google/sanitizers/wiki/AddressSanitizerFlags<!----></a>



<br>





² 



<span class="line"><!---->² <!----></span>





https://pubs.opengroup.org/onlinepubs/9699919799/functions/strdup.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://pubs.opengroup.org/onlinepubs/9699919799/functions/strdup.html"><!---->https://pubs.opengroup.org/onlinepubs/9699919799/functions/strdup.html<!----></a>



<br>





³

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://en.cppreference.com/w/c/string/byte/strndup"><!---->https://en.cppreference.com/w/c/string/byte/strndup<!----></a>



<br>





⁴ 



<span class="line"><!---->⁴ <!----></span>





https://github.com/google/sanitizers/issues/907



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/google/sanitizers/issues/907"><!---->https://github.com/google/sanitizers/issues/907<!----></a>

           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
